<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="physical-chemistry-ii">PHYSICAL CHEMISTRY II<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#physical-chemistry-ii" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="section-1-multiplechoicequestions-40marks">SECTION 1 (MULTIPLECHOICEQUESTIONS) 40MARKS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#section-1-multiplechoicequestions-40marks" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Which of the following property cannot be used to describe the state of a system?
a) pressure
b) volume
c) temperature
d) universal gas constant</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>When work is done on system or by a system there is a change in <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mspace width="2em"></mspace></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\qquad</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0em;"></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 2em;"></span></span></span></span></span>
a) external energy
b) internal energy
c) adiabatic energy
d) isothermal energy</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The system that does not allow the heat to pass through its boundary between the system and surroundings is called as <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mspace width="2em"></mspace></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\qquad</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0em;"></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 2em;"></span></span></span></span></span> system.
a) adiabatic
b) open
c) isothermal
d) close</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>An open system allows the transfer of <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mspace width="2em"></mspace></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\qquad</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0em;"></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 2em;"></span></span></span></span></span>
a) only mass
b) only energy
c) both mass and energy
d) neither mass nor energy</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The temperature of an object increases slowly, then the energy of that object <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mspace width="2em"></mspace></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\qquad</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0em;"></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 2em;"></span></span></span></span></span>
a) increases slowly
b) decreases quickly
c) increases quickly
d) decreases slowly</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Which of the following is an intensive property?
a) Volume
b) Colour
c) Enthalpy
d) Internal energy</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If an exothermic reaction occurs in a Bomb calorimeter then the temperature of the water bath <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mspace width="2em"></mspace></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\qquad</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0em;"></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 2em;"></span></span></span></span></span>
a) increases
b) decreases
c) remains constant
d) cannot predict</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Bomb calorimeter is used to determine
a) molar heat capacity
b) heat of combustion
c) rate kinetics
d) affinity</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The total heat energy utilized for increasing the temperature by 4 degrees Kelvin in a 3 kgs substance is 100 KJ what is the specific heat capacity of that substance?
a) <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>8.34</mn><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">K</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">J</mi></mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">/</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">g</mi><mo>−</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">k</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">8.34 \mathrm{KJ} / \mathrm{g}-\mathrm{k}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span><span class="mord">8.34</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">KJ</span></span><span class="mord">/</span><span class="mord mathrm" style="margin-right: 0.01389em;">g</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">−</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6944em;"></span><span class="mord mathrm">k</span></span></span></span></span>

(b)Differentiate between the energy of fission and the energy of fusion ( 4 mks )
(c) Find the cell potential of a galvanic cell based on the following reduction halfreactions at <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>2</mn><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">∘</mo></msup><mi mathvariant="normal">C</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">2^{\circ} \mathrm{C}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">2</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.6741em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">∘</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mord mathrm">C</span></span></span></span></span></p>

<p>Where <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo stretchy="false">[</mo><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">C</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">d</mi></mrow><mn>2</mn><mo>+</mo><mo stretchy="false">]</mo><mo>=</mo><mn>0.020</mn><mi mathvariant="normal">M</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">[\mathrm{Cd} 2+]=0.020 \mathrm{M}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; <div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="section-1-multiple-choice-questions-40-marks">SECTION 1:MULTIPLE CHOICE QUESTIONS - 40 MARKS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#section-1-multiple-choice-questions-40-marks" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>1 Cobalt-60 decays to nickel-60. What particle is emitted?
A) proton
B) positron
C) Neutron
D) alpha
E) electron
2. Iodine-131 has a half-life of 8.1 days and is used as a tracer for the thyroid gland. If a patient drinks a sodium iodide ( NaI ) solution containing iodine-131 on a Tuesday, how many days will it take for the concentration of iodine-131 to drop to <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>5.0</mn><mi mathvariant="normal">%</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">5.0 \%</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8056em; vertical-align: -0.0556em;"></span><span class="mord">5.0%</span></span></span></span></span> of its initial concentration?
A) 19 days
B) 35 days
C) 0.81 day
D) 4.3 days
E) E 8.1 days
3. Phosphorus-32 is a radioactive isotope used as a tracer in the liver. How much phosphorus32 was originally used if there is only 3.50 mg left in a sample after 288 h ? (The half-life of phosphorus- 32 is 14.3 days.)
A) 1.96 mg
B) 7.00 mg
C) 6.26 mg
D) 17.9 mg
E) 4.17 mg
4. Which one of the following statements is not correct?
A) Carbon-10 is unstable because it has too few neutrons.
B) All nuclides with <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">Z</mi><mo>&gt;</mo><mn>83</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\mathrm{Z}&gt;83</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7224em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mord mathrm">Z</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">&gt;</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">83</span></span></span></span></span> decay into nuclides with smaller Z values.
C) Generally, the number of neutrons in a nuclide is equal to or less than the atomic number.
D) As the atomic number increases, the ratio of neutrons to protons in a nuclide increases.
5. Which of the following statements is typically true for a catalyst?
A) The concentration of the catalyst will go down as the reaction proceeds.
B) The catalyst provides a new pathway in the reaction mechanism.
C) The catalyst speeds up the reaction.
D) Two of the above.
E) None of the above.
6. Consider the rate law: rate <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>=</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">k</mi><mo stretchy="false">[</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">Y</mi><msup><mo stretchy="false">]</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi></msup><mo stretchy="false">[</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">Z</mi><msup><mo stretchy="false">]</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">n</mi></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">=\mathrm{k}[\mathrm{Y}]^{\mathrm{m}}[\mathrm{Z}]^{\mathrm{n}}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.3669em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathrm">k</span><span class="mopen">[</span><span class="mord mathrm" style="margin-right: 0.025em;">Y</span><span class="mclose"><span class="mclose">]</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.6644em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mathrm mtight">m</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mopen">[</span><span class="mord mathrm">Z</span><span class="mclose"><span class="mclose">]</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.6644em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mathrm mtight">n</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>. How are the exponents m and n determined?
A) by using the balanced chemical equation
B) by using the subscripts of the chemical formulas</p>
<p>C) by using the coefficients of the chemical formulas
D) by educated guess
E) by experiment

20. Which of the following statements is false?
A) Breaking weak bonds and making a greater number of equally weak bonds is endothermic.
B) Breaking weak bonds and making an equal number of strong bonds is exothermic.
C) Bond enthalpy values are based on molecules in the gas phase.
D) Bond enthalpies quantify the energy change for the complete separation of two bonded atoms in a molecule at constant pressure.
E) Breaking bonds is always endothermic.
21. Which of the following statements is correct?
A) The internal energy of a system increases when more work is done by the system than heat was flowing into the system.
B) The internal energy of a system decreases when work is done on the system and heat is flowing into the system.
C) The system does work on the surroundings when an ideal gas expands against a constant external pressure.
D) All statements are true.
E) All statements are false.

<ol start="30">
